REPUBLIC OF GUINEA
TRANSPORT SECTOR PROJECT
Transport Sector Investment
1.        In view of the dilapidated state of basic transport infra-
structure, it is important that the transport sector be accorded a high
priority in the allocation of resources, so that it can play its key
role in facilitating economic recovery.   Further, given the overall
needs of Gulnea's economy, it is important not only that funding for
high priority investments be secured, but that funding for non-priority
works be excluded.  Careful identification of essential investments in
the transport sector is therefore imperative. Historically, investments
for public works and transport have fluctuated considerably.  In the
first twelve years following independence, they represented a third of
total public investment expenditure, averaging about US$18 m p.a. (An-
nex 2-11). They went mainly for construction of some 900 km of paved
roads financed through supplier credits provided by foreign contractors,
and for the port and rail infrastructure related to the Bok6 bauxite
mine financed through IBRD loans. A similar level of investment was
maintained during the 1973-84 period, but it represented only 19% of
total public investments on average. Some of this, at IDA's insistence,
went to emergency rehabilitation and maintenance of essential road and
port infrastructure that had become unusable for lack of upkeep, but
considerable sums continued to be spent on projects of little economic
merit, such as Jet-standard airports at Faranah and Kankan, jet air-
craft, inappropriate dredging equipment, railcars, etc. Allocation of
local funds for road maintenance was negligible under the First Republic
and remains so at present.
2.        In the first two years (1985/86) following the advent of the
Second Republic, the Public Investment Program has been largely confined
to ongoing operations and has only embryonically reflected the shift in
priorities resulting from the transformation of Guinea's economy (An-
nex 2-10). With the introduction of a general economic reform program
supported by IDA, the IMF and other international financing agencies,
the bases for more realistic public investment programming have now been
established.  A multilateral debt restructuring was agreed to by the
Paris Club in April 1986 on terms that provided substantial relief on
debt service obligations and accumulated payment arrears up to end-1985.
Unfortunately, Government's revenue outlook from its main source --
bauxite exports - is poor in the short- to medium-term, limiting its
ability to increase its contribution to the financing of its public
investment program.  Guinea will therefore have to rely on external
financing at highly concessionary terms for the important transport
sector investments required in the years ahead.
WAPTR, April 1987

LE SECTEUR DES TRANSPORTS ET LES INFRASTRUCTURES LIEES
A. Les transports routiers
Les enieux
1.        Le reseau comprend 14.000 km de routes classees dont 1.145 km de
routes goudronnees et quelques 9.000 km de pistes sur lesquelles c.rculent
environ 25 000 vehicules, pour la plupart 1lgers et en mauvais etat. Ce
rdseau n'a pas 4td suffisamment entretenu A l'exception de tras rares
troncons de routes principales. De ce fait, la plupart des routes sont dans
un etat d4plorable, rendant tras difficile et par consequent fort cofteux,
l'acces aux centres d'activit4 et en particulier aux exploitations
agricoles et forestieres. Aussi la renovation et la construction des grands
axes et des pistes d'accbs doivent-ell3s Otre considerees comme un
prdalable au d4veloppement de la plupart des activites economiques notam-
ment a dominante rurale.
2.        La rehabilitation et la mise en place des infrastructures
constituent donc une priorite essentielle pour le Gouvernement. Les moyens
qui leur seront consacrds sur la periode 1987-1989 bien qu'insuffisants eu
dgard aux besoins, representent une part tres importante des investisse-
ments publics. Les bailleurs de fonds slinteressant au secteur des
transports seront convies, dans les prochairs mois, a une reunion de
concertation en vue d'harmoniser leurs interventions.
La strat6gie du Gouvernement
3.        A l'exception des transports urbains de masse qui seront domin6s
par des soci4t4s d'economie mixte, le secteur prive prendra en charge les
activitds de transport routier. Les autorites comptent mettre en place le
cadre reglementaire adequat (notamment pour contrbler le poids et la
dimension des vehicules) et prevoient des lignes de credits auprbs des
banques commerciales I destination des entreprises de transport, en vue de
l'acquisition de vehicules et de pibces detachees.
4.        En revanche, l'Etat se doit de mettre & la disposition des
utilisateurs des infrastructures suffisantes et viables. Un plan de trans-
port a 6te realise, qui precise les priorites en matibre de routes princi-
pales et de routes secondaires et ddfinit les etudes de faisabilitd a
engager rapidement en vue d'exdcuter les programmes ultdrieurs.
5.        L'effort porte auJourd'hui sur l'axe Gudkedou-Ser6dou : 126 km de
route pour le desenclavement de la Guin6e Forestire. En 1987, seront
traites les probl&mes lids & la route Conakry-Mamou et au renforcement des
routes bitumees. L'Office des Projets Routiers poursuit un programme de
rehabilitation des routes en terre et organisera l'entretien courant avec
les collectivites locales. Le Secr6tariat d'Etat aux Travaux Publics (SETP)
prepare un programme complementaire pour les ponts en bois. Par ailleurs,
la r4habilitation des rues de Conakry, compte tenu de leur extreme vdtust6,
a Mt4 consid4r6e comme une operation prioritaire. Enfin, les projets

La situation e^tuelle
7.        A Conakry, la GuinEe dispose d'un port complet comprenant une
station min6ralibre, cinq quais de marchandises et des aires pour les
petits bateaux, dont la capacite est insuffisante & moyen tenme. La
structure et l'organisation actuelles n4cessitent des am6liorations. Le
second port en eau profonde, Kamsar, dessert exclusivement lea entreprises
minilres. Enfin, quelques autres petits ports existent tout au long de la
c6te. Au niveau de l'aviation civile, leas am6nagements de l'aeroport
international de Conakry doivent etre termin4s.

C.  Le problem  particulier du chemin de fer

Composante RoutiAre (Road Component)
Contro^le de la v6g6tation, cantonnage
(Vegetation Control and Labor Based Maintenance)
1.        Dans les zones de savane arbor6e et de plateaux secs une
v6g6tation dure et tres dense se developpe sur les accotements.  Cette
vegetation pousse de quatre matres par an r6duisant ainsi la visibilit6.
Elle s'effondre sous son propre poids rendant le r.seau de drainage
inefficace; elle ronge aussi les bords bitumes de la chauss6e. La solu-
tion  traditionnelle  qul  consiste   a  bruler  la  v6g6tation  est
anti-6cologique, dangereuse, nuisible pour le bitume de la chaussge et,
en plus, contreproductive car la vegetation repousse avec une vigueur
accrue. L'autre solution, egalement traditionnelle consiste A couper
manuellement au coupe-coupe cette vegetation deux fois par an. Cette
v6g6tation etant trgs dure, les rendements sont faibles, de l'ordre de
100 m2 par homme-jour.  Les tentatives d'exgcution du debroussaillement
en r6gie n'ont qu'un succes eph6mere, cou'tent cher et sont difficiles
dans les zones peu peupl4es (Kissidougou-Kankan, par exemple); aussi,
leur 4chec  empSche la poursuite d'autres  operations  importantes de
cantonnage (curage des caniveaux, nettoyage des buses, etc.).
2.        Apres consultation avec le Services des Eaux et Forets, du
Jardin Botanique et de l'Agriculture, il apparatt que la seule facon de
reduire le d6veloppement de ces herbes est de les asperger avec un
desherbant (A raison de 9-10 litres par hectare), iummediatement apres la
coupe.  La coupe des vegetaux doit e^tre executee avec des d6broussail-
leuses portatives qui pernmettent un rendement de 1000 m2 par homme-jour,
et egalement avec un broyeur actionn4 par un tracteur agricole (quand la
gdomitrie des accotements le permet, et quand la densite des termitiAres
dures comme du beton ne s'y oppose pas).
3.        Ce contr8le de la vgetation est une operation simple, mais
qui constitue un prealable technique A la mise en place d'un systAtme de
cantonnage sur lea routes bitum6es. Le projet financera une operation
pilote sur la route Kissidougou-Kankan (190 km), zones de savanes peu
boisees, peu peuplees et o4 la v6g6tation extre^mement agressive a r6duit
la largeur de la chaussee de 7 m A 3 m A certains endroits. Les travaux
devront etre executes par un petit entrepreneur qui sera s6lectionn6 et
assiste par le Projet qui lui passera un contrat d'un an. Le projet
achatera directement,  par l'intermidiaire de la centrale d'achat de
1'OPR, les 6quipements et produits qui seront remis A l'entrepreneur et
deduits de sa facturation. L'assistance technique de specialistes en
botanique sera sollicitee pour conseiller et observer lee r6sultats. Un
rapport circonstancig sur l'op6ration sera 6labor6.

REPUBLIQUE DE GUINEE
PROJET SECTORIEL DES TRANSPORTS
Composante Portuaire: Aspects Techniques
Port Subsector: Engineering Aspects
1.        At present, neither the leading channel to Conakry Port nor
the port water area are protected agalnst littoral currents that pass
from north to south through two openings between the existing break-
vaters (Map IBRD 20075). The current, reaching about two knots, depos-
its large quantities of fine sand, silt and clay in the channel and in
front of the deep water berths and has reduced the depth in the channel
from 8.5 m to 7.5 m, in front of the general cargo berths from 8.0 m to
6.5 m, and in front of the bauxite berth from 11.0 m to 7.5 m (35 cms in
the channel and 1.2 m in front of the bauxite berth annually). Closing
the two openings between breakwaters by constructing a siltation preven-
tion dike will reduce maintenance dredging to a minimum, especially in
the port water area, and allow continuous use of quays by bigger ves-
sels,  during all tide  conditions.   Dredging works  financed by the
proposed project will increase the depth of the leading channel to
9.5 m; widen the channel in front of the proposed container berth from
150 m to 250 m to allow for safe turning of the container and Ro-Ro
vessels; and deepen the port water area to -9.5 m. About 1.2 million ms
will be dredged in the channel and 560,000 m' in the port water area.
2.        Adequate information on soil condition at all sites of the
proposed project is available as a result of thorough investigations
carried out during preparation of the port master plan and complemented
by additional recent soil investigations that were needed for the design
of the container berth and the fuel jetty.
3.        Soil condition along the length of the proposed dike is known
to be of soft clay down to -7.0 to -9.0 m. The clay will be dredged
(about 350,000 ml) and replaced by sand. The least-cost solution for
the dike is the rubble mound type with a crest at +4.0 m using about
250,000 ms of stones of different sizes. The dike will be protected by
granite rocks of one to three tons weight.
4.        The proposed fuel Jetty will be locatud east of the OBK
bauxite berth and on the same alignment.  Soils at the site are soft
clays down to -8 to -11 a.  The jetty will consist of a platform to
carry the unloading arms, four breasting dolphins and four mooring
dolphins connected together by a catwalk. The four breasting dolphins
will allow tankers ranging between 1,000 and 30,000 dwt (90 to 190 m
long) to berth. The platform and the eight dolphins will be of tubular
steel piles driven to an appropriate depth in the sand strata underlying
the soft strata. About 650,000 m9 of soft material will be dredged in
front of the jetty to provide the necessary depth for berthing and
turning oil tankers.
5.        The proposed container berth will be located west of the
FRIGUIA miteral berth and on the same alignment.  Soil condition at the
site is known to be good except for about 100 m adjacent to FRIGUIA
berth, where special precautionary measures need to be taken. Several
alternative designs were studied and the least-cost solution was found
to be that using concrete blocks with stone and sand back filling. The



- 96 -                    ANNEX 4-5
Page 2 of 2
filling will reclaim an open storage area of about 75,000 m2 of which
45,000 m2 will be paved under the proposed project. The above-mentioned
precautionary measures wolild include loading the concrete blocks with a
surcharge during berth construction, until final settlement is attained.
However, contractors may also submit alternative designs using other
methods of construction.   The access road to the berth (500 m long)
needs rehabilitation and widening; this is included in the proposed
project. About 225,000 m9 of soil will be dredged to reach a depth of
-12 m, thus allowing for a two meter thick stone foundation under the
concrete blocks.   The new berth is basically protected against wave
action by the island of Kassa and the Prudente breakwater.  However,
there iay be times when waves passing between the island and the break-
water could present a minor hazard. In order to ensure that loading and
unloading of containers are safe under all wave conditions, the consul-
tants who prepared the project carried out a mathematical model study to
assess whether the "Prudente" has to be extended and by how much. Based
on the study, the project includes the extension of the breakwater by
200 m.
WAPTR
April 1987

REPUBLIQUE DE GUINEE
PROJET SECTORIEIJ DES TRANSPORTS
Composante Portuaire: Aspects Institutionnel
Port Sub-Sector: Institutional Strengthening
1.        Although there have been considerable improvements in port
operations over the past two years, cargo handling productivity in
Conakry is still well below that currently achieved in the ports of
Dakar, Abidjan and Douala. In part, this reflects a different crmposi-
tion of the fleets serving these major ports (larger, more modern
vessels with more containerized and pre-palletized cargos, etc.); in
part, however, it reflects a less efficient organization of cargo
handling activities. In some ports, these are carried out by competing
private operators, while they have been handled by state monopolies in
Conakry.  Indifferently organized, insufficiently equipped, and with a
poorly motivated staff on civil service salaries of US$25-60 equivalent
per   month,   these   public   enterprises   barely   coped   with   the
200-220,000 tpy of imported general merchandise in the early 1980s; they
were quite unable to handle the steeply increased traffic of the past
two years (increase of 1986 over 1983 = 180%). In accordance with newly
announced Government policies, private operators were admitted starting
in 1985: first in freight handling and customs clearance; then also for
shiphand3ing and stevedoring. They were given, on an ad-hoc and tempo-
rary basis, licenses as "sub-contractors" to the state enterprises
which, legally, had the exclusive right to operate in the port: SNG for
consignment, PAC for stevedoring, and ENTRAT for freight and customs
handling.   The  private  "sub-contractors"  used  their  own  equipment,
employed mostly staff of the existing public enterprises, paying them
private sector wages and demanding and getting outputs comparable with
those in the well-functioning ports in the region. These pilot opera-
tions clearly demonstrated the potential productivity gains and invest-
ment economies (the stevedoring and other companies are responsible for
providing, operating, and maintaining needed Cargo handling equipment in
addition to those now owned by PAC or ENTRAT) achievable through priva-
tization, although the absence of well-defined ground rules for private
sector participation created a somewhat ambiguous situation as regards
the technical and financial obligations of the public enterprises and of
private operators.
2.        During preparation  of  the  proposed  project,  IDA  and  the
co-financiers have assisted SET and PAC in developing a regulatory
framework for full-scale privatization of7 port-associated services.
Draft regulations concerning "Le Travail des Dockers," "le Consigna-
taire," "le Manutentionnaire," "le Transitaire," "l'Agent en Douane," et
"les Courtiers de Navire," are in the project file.   Draft revised
Statutes of PAC reflecting the new arrangements and new port regulations
were discussed during appraisal and will be implemented before credit
effectiveness.  This was confirmed during negotiations.
3.        Since PAC has until now been responsible for general port
administration as well as for all harbormaster and stevedoring func-
tions, present port tariffs were designed to generate sufficient port
revenues overall to ensure full financial viability of PAC without,
however, correctly reflecting the costs of the various sub-activities.



- 98 -
ANNEX 4-6
Page 2 of 2
Before transferring responsibility for certain port-associated services
to the private sector, it was essential that a new tariff structure be
developed which allows correct remuneration of operators for services
rendered, while at the same time generating the revenues required for
PAC to cover the cost of its operations as well as debt service on the
past as well as on the proposed loans. During project preparation, a
tariff study was carried out to establish new port tariffs reflecting
(a) the impact of devaluation of the Guinean currency; and (b) the
relative  costs attributable  to different  types of activity and to
different types of users (a copy of the tariff study is in the project
file).  The new tariffs were agreed during negotiations and the decree
establishing new tariffs is expected to be published in May 1987.
4.        During preparation and implementation of the important organ-
izational changes foreseen over the next few years, PAC will continue to
have the technical support of a team of advisers financed by GTZ (Feder-
al Republic of Germany). The latter have agreed to extend the initial
grant for technical assistance (225 m-m) under the Conakry Port Project
for another three-year period (200 m-m) starting April 1986.  Changes in
the composition of the team due to the transfer to the private sector of
certain functions previously carried out by PAC were discussed and
agreed with PAC and GTZ. Particular emphasis will be put on strengthen-
ing operations and financial management, through improved collection of
revenues, computerization of operational and accounting data, and on
developing a system for correct maintenance of the newly rehabilitated
port infrastructure and superstructure.
5.        At present, PAC depends completely on the contractor who is
responsible for the Conakry Port Project to carry out all maintenance
works,  even the very simple ones.   That contractor is expected to
complete his work in mid 1987, after which date maintenance will stop
completely. Agreement was thus reached with PAC during appraisal that
it will sign a contract with an independent experienced contractor
acceptable to the Association under procedures acceptable to the Associ-
ation, to carry out cleaning and maintenance works of all port facili-
ties including navigation aids starting January 1, 1988, under terms and
conditions acceptable to the Association.  This was confirmed during
negotiations.
6,        Hitherto,  the  "Office Maritime"  has been responsible  for
navigation aids in all Guinean ports except Conakry, where they have
been contracted by PAC to maintain navigation aids in working condition.
However, their performance in Conakry has been inadequate and the
majority of these facilities are in extremely poor condition.  It is
thus recommended that, starting January 1, 1988, the contract for
maintenance of navigation aids will also be transferred to the private
contractor referred to in para 5 above. Agreement on this was reached
with the Government during negotiations.
WAPTR
April 1987

REPUBLIQUE DE GUINEE
PROJET SECTORIEL DES TRANSPORTS
Composante Aviation
Aviation Sub-Sector
1.        The responsibilities for management of Guinea's international
airport in Conakry will be transferred to a new Franco-Guinean company,
SOGEAC, with Aeroports de Paris (ADP) as technical partner.  In addi-
tion, a new CCCE project for rehabilitation of the control tower,
partial closure of the airport runway area, and provision of some
equipment,  was approved in  1986.   The difficulties  currently being
experienced in Guinea's aviation activities seem to indicate clearly,
however, that the project of CCCE and ADP which is limited to the
management of Conakry airport's terminal and other ground facilities, is
not sufficient to fully ensure normal operation and safe flying condi-
tions at Conakry; nor does it address the problems of navigation,
meteorological services and of secondary airports for domestic aviation.
Since proper functioning of domestic aviation is particularly important
in the short-term, in order to ensure year-round access to those regions
of the country that do not at present have all-weather road connections,
the proposed project supports a number of actions in the aviation
sub-sector that address institutional problems and complement ongoing
investments by bilateral donors.
2.        Following a study by ICAO and other international consultants,
it has been proposed to establish a new autonomous agency for Air
Navigation and Secondary airports to complement SOGEAC at Conakry and
operate the other airports.  This agency will closely cooperate with
SOGEAC with which it will share some facilities and services in Conakry,
in a manner similar to other airports in the world, where a national
agency provides navigation services while a private or semi-private
organization owns the airport.   The new agency would be financially
autonomous, with revenues derived from airport fees at the secondary
airports and part of the landing fees at Conakry which it would share
with SOGEAC, in a proportion initially estimated at 20/80.
3.        The air navigation agency  (ANA) would be established with
substantial technical assistance to be provided under French bilateral
assistance, as an extension of the CCCE project and ADP assistance to
SOGEAC.  This technical assistance,  estimated at about ten man-years
over the 1988-91 period, would include a mission leader specialized in
air-control, a maintenance expert and a meteorological expert, plus
short-term experts for such matters as telecommunications, rehabilita-
tion of runways for secondary airports, fire fighting, etc.  The de-
tailed program and final composition of this technical assistance,
established in coordination with ADP technical assistance to SOGEAC,
will be specified when the contract for the latter is effective. Terms
of reference of this assistance to the Agency will have to be approved
by the Association. Immediately upon appointment, the technical assis-
tance team will propose the detailed organization, staffing and training
program of the personael of the Agency, which will also have to be
approved by the Association, together with the revenue sharing arrange-
ments with SOGEAC. This was confirmed during negotiations. The Agency
is expected to employ about 70 persons. Most of DAC's existing trained



- 100 -
ANNEX 4-7
Page 2 of 2
personnel is expected to be transferred to SOGEAC and to the Agency. By
early 1992, on the basis of about three years of operation of SOGEAC and
the Agency, a short study should be carried out on the possibility of
merger of the two entities.
4.        Meteorological services for aviation remain the responsibility
of the Meteorologie Nationale, which will, however, detach a team of
about ten key personnel at Conakry, where they will operate under the
guidance  of the ANA.   Similar arrangements would be made  in those
secondary airports where the local Meteorological Observation Centers
are located. These arrangements and those for the maintenance of the
meteorological equipment were agreed upon at negotiations.
5.        An objective of the project is to introduce proper financial
management in the aviation sub-sector. The first step in this direction
has been the establishment of SOGEAC which is to be an autonomous,
financially viable organization. The same objective will be set for the
ANA with emphasis on financial autonomy and recovery of the costs of
investments unde- the project. In particular, the aircraft landing fees
which were not adjusted after the monetary reform of 1986, will have to
be increased at least to levels comparable to those in neighboring
countries. One of the first tasks of the technical assistance to the
ANA in coordination with SOGEAC will be to propose such an adjustment,
at the latest for 1988. During the project implementation period, ANA
will be asked to submit its annual budget for review and comments by the
Association.
6.        A study is being carried out under the PPF on tt,e restructur-
ing of AIR GUINEE. At negotiations, the Government and IDA agreed on a
program of additional studies to be completed by October 1987 on the
basis of which a detailed action plan for restructuring the airline
would be agreed upon.  In particular, specific proposals will be re-
quested from foreign airlines, some of which have already expressed
interest in being associated with the restructured airline. The first
objective of the restructuring will be to make the airline financially
viable, without Government subsidies.  Of primary concern will be the
arrangements for domestic flights. The Government will begin implement-
ing the action plan at latest by June 1988.

REPUBLIC OF GUINEA
TRANSPORT SECTOR PROJECT
Estimations d6taillAes des couts par composante
(Detailed Project Cost Estimates by Component)
Road Component
1.        The total cost  of the road component  including  taxes and
contingencies is estimated at US$35.3 m.  The foreign exchange cost is
US$29.4 m  or  83%  of  the  total  project  cost.   The  local  cost  is
FG 2,336 million, equivalent to US$5.8 m at the present exchange rate.
Taxes will be levied only on local labor and represent less than one
percent.  Costs of works and services are based on recent civil works
contracts, consultant and mission estimates. Physical contingencies of
20% have been allowed against the likelihood that part of the sections
now foreseen for resurfacing may need to be re-constructed.   Annual
price contingencies have been provided for all project items in accor-
dance with trends from documented sources as follows:
Calendar Year
1987      1988      1989      1990     1991
Local Expenditures     15%        15%       15%       15%      15%
Foreign Expenditures    3%        1%        1%        1%       3.5%
2.        The cost estimates for the different types of road rehabilita-
tion works are detailed in Annex 4-1, Table 2.  They amount to about
US$10,000 km for single surface treatment, US$18,000 km for double
surface treatment, and US$82,000 km for full pavement reconstruction.
Drainage works are estimated to average US$3,800 km and preliminary
works such as patching and limited earthworks are estimated at
US$5,200 km. The cost estimates for the pilot vegetation control works
are detailed in Annex 4-2; a provision of 30% for physical contingencies
has been included in view of the experimental nature of this sub-compo-
nent. The average annual cost of about US$210 equivalent per km of road
treated is reasonable. The estimates for rehabilitation of offices and
supply of office equipment are based on similar works and supply con-
tracts  carried  out  recently  in  Conakry.   Rehabilitation works  are
expected to cost US$600/m2 and office equipment and furniture average
US$10,000 per office. The average man-month rate for consultant servi.c-
es for technical assistance or supervision (including salaries, overhead
fees and reimbursable expenses) is estimated at US$14,000.  A summary of
the cost estimates follows.

Composante Rout iere /Road Component
Param6tres de 1'evaluation 6conomigue des renforcements et enduisages
Parameters for the Economic Evaluation of Pavement Strengthening and Resurfacing
1.        The economic evaluation of civil works to be carried out under the project is
based on the Kighway Design and Maintenance Standard Model (HDMS), and more particularly
on the model's evaluation of pavement deterioration processes under specified climatic
conditions and traffic levels. These processes are known to be non-linear, with an
extended initial phase of little manifestation of distress, followed by a phase of rapidly
accelerating deterioration which, in the absence of major periodic maintenance interven-
tion, leads to complete structural failure within five years in all but the most favorable
circumstances. This non-linear behavior of pavement deterioration is critical in the
determination of optimal maintenance strategies for paved roads. Estimated pavement
deterioration rates for Guinea are in Table 5-1, 1 below.
2.        Of the road sectiors to be rehabilitated under the project, only 23% do not show
significant problems. Some 20% exhibit manifestations of beginning pavement failure while
57% have already reached the phase of distress. These sections have been assigned corre-
sponding average roughness indices of (a) IRI - 4; (b) IRI - 5; and (c) IRI - 8, respec-
tively, which indicate the need for different rehabilitation techniques: single surface
or double surface treatments for (a) and (b), and full pavement reconstruction for (c).
3. Scenario de degradation des chaussees en Guinee/Pavement Deterioration Scenario for
Paved Roads in Guinea

- 116 -
ANNEX 5-3
Page 1 of 13
REPUBLIC OF GUINEA
TRANSPORT SECTOR PROJECT
Port Traffic Forecasts
and Economic Evaluation of the Port Component
1.        As  indicatr'I in Annex 2-6,  p. 3,  traffic  at  the Port  of
Conakry which had gro   very little for over a decade up to 1982, has
increased substantially over the past four years to a total of 4.7 m
tons in 1986. Growth was mainly in imports, while export volume (baux-
ite and alumina) stagnated due to the depressed conditions of the world
market. The explosive increase in general merchandise imports, over the
past two years in particular (from 320,000 tons in 1984 to 580,000 tons
in 1986), reflects a combination of factors:  foremost, the opening of
Guinea's economy following the 1984 change of regime, and secondly, the
vastly improved operational capacity of the port following rehabilita-
tion of essential quay and storage facilities, and renewal of floating
and handling equipment. Conditions should stabilize over the next five
year period, during which Guinea's GDP is expected to grow at about
4% p.a., and when foreign exchange availability will constrain the
country's overall volume of imports. Even so, the proportion of con-
tainerized merchandise in total imports is expected to continue growing
disproportionately. Also, Government's emphasis on agricultural devel-
opment should lead to significant growth in agricultural exports, but
these start from a very modest level of about 10,000 tpy at present.
Little growth in mineral exports can be expected in the short-to-medium
term. The traffic forecasts used for the economic analysis assume that
growth in import3 will slow to the rate of GDP growth (4% p.a.) for
1987-95,  and decline  to  3.5% p.a.  thereafter  (Annexes 2-6 and  6-3,
Table 1 give details).
2.        The ERR was calculated for the port component as a whole and
for  the  three main  sub-components:   (a) siltation prevention  dike,
establishment dredging and rehabilitation of navigational aids; (b) the
deepwater container terminal and minor rehabilitation works; and (c) the
fuel jetty).
A. Cost Parameters
3.        Cost estimates for civil works and dredging, and for operation
and maintenance of the new facilities provided under the project were
established by consultants, based on actual costs under the Conakry Port
project adjusted to January 1987 prices, and on comparable costs in

(ii) Reduced ship-waiting time attributable to dredging in
front of the quays:
8.        Before construction of the siltation prevention dike, observed
average ship-waiting time due to dredging before the quays has been
about four months per year.
(a)  Dredging  in  front  of  the  bauxite  quay  (08/09)  requires
0.5 months at a minimum. Given the full occupancy of the quay
year round, this would reduce bauxite exports from 3 million
tpy to 2,875,000 tpy, resulting in annual export losses of
US$25 x 125,000 - US$3,125,000.
(b)  Dredging in front of the othe. quays, if done efficiently
(which has not been the case with the state dredging company
SOMIDRAT), would still require at least two months per year,
resulting in ship-waiting time of at least 60 ship-days. At a
conservatively estimated average cost of US$7,500/day for
ships waiting at the port, annual avoided costs due to reduced
dredging time can be estimated at
US$7,500 x 60 - US$ 450,000
+ (a) above   US$3,125,000
Total           US$3,575,000

11.       Shipping costs per ton per trip are reduced from US$10 to
US$9.05 following maintenance dredging and from US$9.05 to US$8.30 due
to establishment dredging.   (The latter will also reduce lay-over time
of ships that can now only leave port at high tide; this benefit has not
been quantified). For average annual bauxite exports of three million
tons, total savings in transport costs are US$27,140.000 - 24,830,000 -
US$2,310,000.   These  savings,  accruing  to  the  shippers  or bauxite
importers, will be partially appropriated by the Guinean economy through
significantly  higher  port  charges  on bauxite.   The  annual  savings
accruing to the Guinean economy are estimated at half the total savings
or US$1,160,000.
12.       Similar  savings will be  realized by FRIGUIA carriers  and
tankers, as well as by modern container and ro-ro ships that have begun
serving Conakry, but can now do so only on the return trip after they
have unloaded part of their cargo at other ports further down the coast.
Since this traffic cannot at present be estimated correctly, its bene-
fits have not been quantified, although they may prove to be consider-
able.
(iv) Benefits of improved navigational aids:
13.       By enabling ships to safely pass through the access channel
and dock after darkness, a better utilization of quays (two shift
system) will become feasible. The main benefit of proper signalization,
however, is the prevention of shipwrecks in the access channel, which
could block all port operations (an ore carrier actually ran aground in
the channel in December 1986, but could be freed by tugs at high tide
after three days). Since these benefits are difficult to estimate, they
have been assumed, conservatively, to be no more than the costs of the
investment.
14.       The table summarizing costs and benefits for subcomponent (a)
is on page 10. The calculated ERR is 22%.
Subcomponent (b)
(i) Avoided ship waiting time due to increased port
capacity and expedited berthing
15.       The commercial port currently disposes of four full quays:
quays 02-05, with a total length of only 480 m, are considered as three
quays, while quays 01 (FRTGUIA) and 07 (fishing vessels) are only 50%
available for handling general merchandise.  In the "without project"
case, the following daily and annual tonnages can be handled:

16.       Based on the traffic projections for the port (Annex 2-6 and
Annex 6-3, Table 1), quay occupancy rates would be close to 100% up to
1990 and exceed 100% thereafter, resulting in infinite ship waiting
time. Part of the traffic would therefore have to be diverted to the
nearest neighboring port - Freetown in Sierra Leone -- from where goods
would have to be transported by road to Conakry.   Traffic would be
diverted when ship-waiting costs (estimated at US$7,500/day) exceed the
cost of road transport (estimated at US$30/ton). According to a formula
established by UNCTAD ("Berth Throughput," 1973), this would be the case
for volumes above 570,000 tpy corresponding to a quay occupancy rate of
about 73%. Conservatively, the analysis assumes that traffic would only
be diverted at quay occupancy rates above 85%, equivalent to an annual
port handling capacity of 638,000 tons.
17.       In the "with project" case, port capacity would be substan-
tially increased by the provision of a new container terminal to be
managed by private operators, and by further rehabilitation works of
existing port facilities. Following completion of the container termi-
nal, existing port facilities are expected to handle conventional
merchandise at a rate of 575 t per day per quay while the new container
terminal could handle up to 3,000 t of containerized cargo per day based
on two shifts/day. With a 75% occupancy rate for the existing quays and
a 45% occupancy rate of the container terminal quay, annual port capaci-
ty in 1991 would be:
4 x 300 x   575 x 0.75 - 520,000 t
1 x 300 x 3.000 x 0.45 - 405,000 t
TOTAL                     925,000 t
and traffic would be diverted only if total general merchandise imports
and exports exceeded this volume.

(ii)  Reduction in losses due to improved security in a
separate and privately-managed container terminal:
19.        Although port rehabilitation and especially construction of a
custom-wall and provision of floodlighting have contributed to a reduc-
tion of the extremely high pilferage rates in Conakry Port, the problem
is  far  from  eradicated.   To  avoid  security  problems,  shippers  are
increasingly containerizing goods that normally would not be (sugar,
cars, etc.) since pilferage from containers is significantly lower the.n
for general  cargo.   The new container  terminal will make  container
handling much more efficient, promote containerized traffic, and thus
reduce losses through breakage and pilferage significantly. Assuming an
average cargo value of US$650/ton of general merchandise imported, a
conservatively estimated reduction of losses by no more than one per-
cent, would result in the following savings:

and warehousing costs for importers, these have been disregarded in the

Subcomponent (c)
22.       Over 80% of all petroleum products imported into Guinea pass
through Conakry port (the remainder, mainly for Bok6 mine consumption,
being off-loaded at Kamsar).  ONAH storage facilities are situated to
the east of the port area.  Currently, oil tankers have to use the
alumina (01) and bauxite (08) quays to discharge fuel, both for FRIGUIA
and OBK use, and for ONAH.
23.       Two considerations have been uppermost in the decision to
construct a fuel jetty: the first is operational safety; the second, to
relieve  present  congestion and attendant  ship waiting time on the
mineral quays. Under current operating conditions, fire hazards are an
ever-present danger:  no fire protection is available at the mineral
quays, where missions have observed open-flame welding going on while a
tanker was discharging. The damage of a single fire -- if it destroyed
the bauxite unloading facilities and interrupted bauxite exports for
several months -- could easily reach US$10-15 m in foregone exports
alone, without counting the cost of replacing the destroyed facilities
and clearing up soil and water pollution. However, while safety con-
cerns are the main reasons for constructing the new facility, they can
not be adequately quantified, and have thus been disregarded in the ERR
calculation.
24.       As presented, the ERR for the fuel jetty is based mainly on
the savings due to reduced congestion of the mineral quays. At present,
quay 01 is occupied for at least 35 days per year for fuel discharge:
during this time, it could alternatively serve to handle some
21,000 tons of general merchandise, which would thus not have to be
diverted.   The resulting benefits are estimated at 21,000 x US$30 -
US$630.000/yr.  Concerning quay 08, its present occupancy rate is 92%.
Since oil tankers take precedence over ore-carriers, the resulting ship
waiting time amounts to some 70 ship days at a minimum, with associated
costs of 70 x US$7,500 - US$525,000/yr.
25.       A  further  quantifiable  saving  would  result  from  avoided
replacement costs for the pipeline between the FRIGUIA terminal
(quay 01) and the fuel depot. This pipeline is failing (with resultant
additional fire hazards in the commercial port areas) and would have to
be replaced at an estimated cost of US$1.25 million.
26.       The table summarizing costs and benefits for subcomponent (c)
is on page 12; the calculated ERR is 12%.
27.       The overall ERR for the port component (page 13) for the base
case presented above is 24%. Decreasing benefits by 20% reduces the ERR
to 20% overall; increasing costs by 20% results in an overall ERR of



- 125 -
ANNEX 5-3
Page 10 of 13
21%. Even if benefits decreased and costs increased by 20% respective-
ly, the ERR would remain satisfactory at 17%.

REPUBLIC OF GUIN!A
TRANSPORT SECTOR PROJECT
Financial Evaluation of PAC
A. Recent Financial Performance and Current Financial Position
1.        PAC's summary income account and cash flow statements, includ-
ing actual data for 1983 to 1985 and estimates for 1986, are summarized
in the table below and detailed in Table 1.  From its constitution in
1982 through 1986, PAC has been carrying out all stevedoring and
on-shore handling activities, which are reflected in its revenues and
expenses.  PAC's accounts were denominated in sylis until 1985.  Since
the monetary reform in January 1986, which included a thirteen-fold
devaluation,  they are denominated  in Guinean  francs.   PAC's opening
accounts for 1986 were revaluated to reflect devaluation.
PAC's Summary Income and Cash Flow Statements
Actual                    Estimate
(in million Sylis)          (in million FC)
1983       1984       1985            1986
operating Revenues              232.4      397.3      438.1          4,430.3
Working Expenses                115.9      106.2      179.3            970.9
Depreciation and Provisions      61.4      108.8       78.1          1,431.2
Net Operating Revenue            55.1      182.3      180.7          2,028.2
Interest Charges                (1.7)       22.5       43.8          1,286.8
Extraordinary Gain (Loss)        33.8      (11.6)      (9.7)        (2,136.9)
Net Income/Loss after Taxes      55.0       96.3       82.6         (1,395.5)
Internal Cash Generation       110.9       153.0      156.7           342.2
Working Ratio (%)               50          27         41              22
Operating Ratio (%)              76         55         58              54
The revenue and cash flow objectives set for the implementation period
of the First Port Project were generally achieved, thanks to larger than
expected traffic volumes, adequate tariff revisions and low working
expenses,  including  very  low  personnel  costs.   The  1986  estimates
indicate a net loss despite a large net operating revenue, because of
exceptional  losses  and  provisions.   These  include  foreign  exchange
losses following the 1986 devaluation, a provision for deferred mainte-
nance dredging and especially a large (US$3 m) provision for losses on
long outstanding receivables from foreign shipping companies.  On the
whole, PAC's net income after taxes has averaged US$1.5 m on annual
revenues averaging US$14.6 m over the 1983-86 period. Cumulated inter-
nal cash generation over the period reached US$18.9 m, allowing PAC to
finance the local cost of the first Port Project, build its working
capital at the required levels and, after deduction of financial charges
during construction and provisions for dredging, accumulate a net cash
surplus of US$7.7 million.

PAC's December 1985 balance sheet was fully revaluated by its Auditors;
their work included a detailed evaluation of fixed assets and was a
first of its kind for a Public Enterprise in Guinea. The revaluation
surplus amounted to FG 2,286 million. The results of this revaluation
are being agreed with the Ministry of Finance. Concurrently with the
revaluation, it has been assumed that in the December 31, 1986 balance
sheet, PAC's equity would be reduced by FG 1,600 million, as land and
old buildings which were part of the initial Government contribution
would be taken out of PAC's fixed assets.
3.        From 1983 to 1985, PAC's net accounts receivable increased
substantially to FG 2,974 million by December 1985, or more than nine
months' revenues. These include arrears of local clients, mostly public
enterprises and the administration, as well as by foreign port users.
The largest debtors among the latter were the Eastern European shipping
companies carrying bauxite exports, who have consistently paid their
debts, but have done so erratically and with considerable delays; they
also include other small companies, often trampers, which were carrying
most of the general cargo to Conakry before the large liners restarted
regular service in late  1985 and 1986.   Billings have been greatly
handicapped by the fact that PAC had to collect them through the prob-
lem-ridden parastatal Socigth Navale Guin4enne (SNG) which was the only
authorized shipping agent and consignee.   In addition, monitoring of
actual payments by foreign clients has been hampered by poor telecommu-
nications and by the fact that transfers of funds were generally per-
formed through the old state banks which had very poor bookkeeping and
abysmal losses. The liquidation of these banks in 1986, as well as the
poorly managed restructuring of SNG, has further added to the confusion.
Finally, PAC's financial and accounting department has had difficulties



- 131 -                    ANNEX 6-1
Page 3 of 12
in dealing with this complex situation and with the fast growth of
traffic, partly because specific technical assistance to the financial
department was too long delayed. Several corrective measures were taken
in  1986.   PAC appointed  the Hamburg Port  Consulting  to completely
overhaul foreign client accounts and collect arrears prior to 1986. In
addition, PAC introduced new payment procedures including advance
payments and deposits by shippers, and started applying stringent
measures including detaining delinquent ships.  As a result,  actual
collection (including arrears) during 1986 on foreign clients reached
US$8.4 m against total billings of US$9.2 m.  Total gross receivables
thereby increased only by 16% to Gi? 5,121 million by December 1986,
while total revenues increased by 36%.
4.        PAC's current assets as of December 1986 include large amounts
deposited and frozen in the liquidated state banks, of which US$8.6 m in
foreign currency. The unavailability of these sums has so far made it
impossible for PAC to have long overdue maintenance dredging carried out
by a foreign contractor. Also, PAC has not yet paid to the Treasury the
interest during construction on the loans for the first Port Project and
some taxes, which constitute the bulk of its current liabilities.
B. Tariffs
5.        Under the ongoing Port Project, a new tariff structure was put
into effect in 1984, which essentially included port dues on ships and
stevedoring charges payable in dollars, and wharf-handling and storage
charges for cargo, payable in local currency (for details see An-
nex 6-2). Regular tariff increases were implemented over 1984-85; and
following the 1986 devaluation, an intermediate revision of tariffs
payable in local currency was introduced, which compensated partly for
the effect of the devaluation. However, tariff adjustments on bauxite
and alumina shipments could not be implemented: the mining companies,
who incurred substantial losses because of insufficient dredging which
allowed only smaller ore-carriers or partially loaded larger ships to
use the port, have refused to pay the tariff increase during 1986.
6.        Further adjustments of the tariff structure are required in
1987 to reflect: (a) the transfer of the stevedoring, shorehandling and
warehousing activities from PAC to private sector operators, thereby
transforming PAC into an organization dealing essentially with infra-
structure; (b) the changed and evolving structure of the traffic to
Conakry with a higher proportion of large modern container ships and
ro-ro vessels carrying fast-growing volumes of unitized cargo; (c) the
necessity to fully recover in the future the cost of the different
investments in the proposed port extension under the project, with
charges corresponding more accurately to the cost of services which the
different users and types of cargo will receive from the new port with
its new installations and institutional set-up; and (d) a factor for
time-of-occupancy of berth in the tariffs, to encourage fast throughput.
A new tariff structure prepared by a consultant was reviewed with the
Association before negotiations and found acceptable. At the same time,
reference tariffs are being proposed for the operations taken over by
the private sector. On the whole, port charges plus stevedoring tariffs
would increase by about 28% over the 1986 levels on average. PAC's new
tariffs are expected to be put into effect at the latest by June 1987.
To achieve the financial objectives specified below, regular subsequent



- 132 -                 ANNEX 6-1
Page 4 of 12
tariff increases will be required.  The tariff structure will be re-
viewed again with the Association at the opening of the new container
terminal.
C. Financial Objectives
7.        PAC's stated objective is to be a fully autonomous, commer-
cially-oriented and profitable public enterprise.   Its statutes, cur-
rently adapted in line with the privatization process, specify that
operating revenues should cover all operating expenses, including
adequate maintenance expenditures, interest charges on debt, provision
for losses and renewals, and a minimum return of 6% on reevaluated net
fixed assets.  The authorities have consistently accepted tariff in-
creases requested by PAC to achieve stated objectives, but PAC's manage-
ment has tended to make inadequate provision for losses. Proper estima-
tion of these and setting of adequate salaries and incentives for
personnel will need special attention in the annual budget preparation
process. As under the first Port Project, PAC will be required, during
the project implementation period, to submit annual draft budgets for
comment by the Association.
8.        Progress toward financial autonomy for PAC has been less than
satisfactory with regard to control by the Government of PAC's opera-
tional expenditures and Bank accounts.  At present, all expenditures
above FG 200,000 are submitted to a priori Government control, making
the timely execution of maintenance very difficult. Also, in addition
to the regulation whereby PAC's cash surplus was to be deposited in
non-interest-bearing accounts in the Central Bank, the Government
requested in 1986 that payments by PAC's clients be effected directly
into Central Bank accounts, which makes monitoring of client accounts
extremely cumbersome. At negotiations, the Government agreed to replace
a priori control by a posteriori control for all operating expenses as
well as investments, for contracts not exceeding US$250,000. Similarly,
PAC will be allowed to (a) maintain accounts at commercial banks; and
(b) keep its surpluses in interest-bearing accounts.
9.        As mentioned in para 3, PAC's financial management needs to be
reinforced. The recent recruitment of a high-level financial expatriate
advisor, previously financial manager of the Port of Abidjan, is already
a major step towards  this reinforcement.   With his help,  PAC will
prepare a detailed program covering the strengthening of the accounting
system, the setting up of fail-safe billing procedures based on depend-
able information using a new computer system; the introduction of proper
internal controls; and the corresponding training of key personnel
abroad. Agreement of this program by the Association will be a condi-
tion of effectiveness. Its major immediate objective will be to improve
collection  of  receivables.   Significant  progress  has  already  been
achieved during the first quarter of 1987, as monthly collections
averaged 118% on billings on foreign clients and 102% on all billings.
The transfer of all stevedoring, ship consignment and especially for-
warding/custom clearing activities to private firms by April 1987, will
further improve collections, as PAC will henceforth have to deal only
with a small number of selected firms of good standing, based in
Conakry.



- 133 -                  ANNEX 6-1
Page 5 of 12
10.       Other agreements under the ongoing Port Project on financial
targets and covenants, reevaluation of assets and annual audits, and
agreement of the Association on PAC's investment expenditures during
project implementation, are being reconducted under the new project.
Financial targets agreed upon are as follows:
Financial Ratios
(a)  Working ratio:       1988 and beyond: not to exceed 60%
(b)  Operating ratio:    1988 and beyond: not to exceed 80%
(c)  Kate of return:      1988 and beyond: minimum 6% on revalued
net fixed assets in use
(d)  Cur nt ratio:       minimum 20
(e)  Debt service         after project completion, minimum 1.25
coverage ratio:
Working Capital
-- Minimum cash:    two months of working expenses
-- Receivables:     not to exceed three months' revenues
-- Inventories:     not to exceed six months' spare parts needs for
the coming year, nor fall below three months'
needs
-- Accounts         not to exceed three months' supplier accounts
payable:        and other current payables.
11.       As mentioned in paras 3 and 4, GF 3,719 m (US$9.3 m) of PAC's
cash, mostly in foreign exchange, have been frozen in the liquidated
state banks, and similarly about GF 733 m is due to PAC by the State,
mostly state enterprises (some of which are being liquidated, but also
fishing concerns which have never paid their port dues) and adminis-
tration departments.  In addition, PAC should also collect through the
State about US$3.1 m of arrears from some foreign shipping lines, mostly
the bauxite carriers, that have to be negotiated under bilateral ar-
rangements.  Conversely, PAC owes to the state GF 2,648 m in interest
during construction on the loans for the Port Project, and GF 511 m in
tax arrears. PAC has prepared a plan for compensation of those recipro-
cal debts, which was finalized and agreed upon with the Ministry of
Finance before negotiations. This plan also includes: (a) compensation
for PAC's foregone revenues of GF 174 m for the period of 1986 and 1987
during which the mining companies refused to pay announced tariff
increases; and (b) GF 557 m in foregone interest, as PAC's surplus was
frozen in non-interest-bearing accounts.  The balance of GF 3,375 m in
favor of PAC will be used in 1987 to prepay 21% (equivalent to US$8.4 m)
of the outstanding loans for the First Project, thereby reducing future
debt service to acceptable levels and improving PAC's debt-equity ratio.
Completion of all legal documentation for implementation of the restruc-
turing plan will be a condition of effectiveness.



- 134 -                  ANNEX 6-1
Page 6 of 12
12.       In addition to the debt compensation, the. Government agreed at
negotiations to:  (a) consolidate as equity the former liability la-
belled "depreciation to be paid to the Plan" by PAC under the old ac-
counting system; and (b) allow PAC to carry forward cumulated losses (as
determined on the basis of the 1985 and 1986 reevaluated financial
statements) before paying income taxes.
D. Forecast Financial Performance
13.       The  financial  forecasts  for the  1987/95 period have been
developed taking into account the fact that PAC relinquished all steve-
doring  activities  to  priva,se  sector  companies  by April 1987.   The
forecasts, in current prices, are based on conservative traffic assump-
tions, stepped tariff increases and major increases of expenditures in
local currency, the levels of which have not yet been fully adjusted
following monetary reform.   Fixed asset values and the depreciation
schedule used are derived from the revaluation for the opening balance
sheet as of December 31, 1985.  Major assumptions and considerations
used in the forecast are detailed in the Project File.
14.       Traffic forecasts used for the financial projections are very
conservative; exports of minerals (bauxite and alumina) are assumed to
remain constant at their 1986 levels (3.4 million dry ton); imports of
oil products and dry bulk products (chemicals, clinker) are supposed to
increase by about 3.7% p.a., and imports of general cargo would increase
by about 4.0% between 1986 and 1995, starting from a volume of
600,000 tons in 1986. Total labor costs in GF are assumed to increase
by 50% from 1986 to 1988, while total personnel would decrease by about
55%.  The assumed increase would compensate for the devaluation and
bring remuneration closer to a level observed in ports in neighboring
countries.   Other operating expenditures are assumed to decrease by
6% p.a. between 1986 and 1987 as PAC is transferring handling equipment
and personnel to the private stevedoring companies. Equipment trans-
ferred to private operators is expected to be sold at its book value.
It is also assumed that PAC will continue to pay high interest rates on
the loans for the Port project (13% for the IDA funds, and 11.5% on the
AfDB loan), but on reduced outstanding amounts as foreseen by the
restructuring plan described in para 11. The forecast income account is
summarized below and detailed in Annex 6-3.

15.        PAC's operating income would be positive all through project
construction and thereafter under this conservative traffic growth
scenario.  Under the assumption that interest on the new loans for the
project are charged to the income statement the same year, net income
would become negative in 1989 without  tariff increase other than the
1987  adjustment.   To  cover  the major  increase  in  financial  charges
between 1988 and 1992 and loan repayments thereafter, a new increase ill
tariffs will thus be needed starting at the latest in 1990. With total
tariff increases of 34% in current terms between 1989 and 1993 (with
5% p.a. in 1989 and 1990, 10% in 1991, and 5% in 1992 and in 1993),
PAC's income after taxes would be slightly positive in 1989-1991, and
become a substantial net profit from 1993 onward, when shipping would
start to fully benefit from the new port facilities. The rate of return
on net fixed assets in use would reach 9% until 1991, and exceed 10%
starting in 1992. If traffic growth exceeds 4% annually, the required
tariff increases would be substantially reduced.

La Including GF 1,700 million of possible prepayment of the loans for the first project, but
which is not taken into account in the debt service ratio calculation.
During the 1987-92 period, PAC would cover with its initial cash surplus
and cash flow, US$11.4 m for maintenance dredging, minimum increases in
working capital needs and the local cost portion of the new project, as
well as some US$59 m in interest during construction and debt service on
the borrowings for the first Port project.  The substantial additional
cash outflow occurring when debt service on the new borrowings will
cumulate with the debt service on the old borrowings, would be covered
thanks to the tariff increases over 1589-92. Again, if traffic increas-
es faster than projected  in this conservative projection,  the needed
tariff increases would be smaller. In the peak year, 1992, 68% of PAC's
cash expenses would be interest paid to the Government on the credits
for the first and second port project .-e-lent at high interest rates.
Even during the two years of maximum cash outflows (1989/90), PAC would
still generate a small net cash surplus. Debt service coverage ratio
would remain at 1.3-1.4 between 1992 and 1995, which is acceptable given
the possibility of waiving the in'ome tax and the comfortable surplus
cash accumulated before  1989.   Once  the project  is completed,  it is
likely that PAC will prepay another portion of the high interest loans
of the first project with its cumulated cash surplus. The above projec-
tion assumes that PAC would prepay GF 1,700 m at the end of 1992.

PAC's actual fixed assets would increase substantially with the imple-
mentation of the new project. Since PAC's cash generation will be used
mostly for repayment of the loans for the first Port Project, and
payment of the maintenance dredging and interest during construction
under the new project, the new investments will be financed mainly by
the  new  loans.   PAC's  long  term  liabilities  would  thereby  increase
substantially until  1991.   Thereafter,  PAC's  debt  equity ratio would
gradually improve as repayments of principal on the new loans add to the
repayments on the earlier loans. Agreement was reached at negotiations
on a debt limitation covenant, excluding any additional long-term debt
during project implementation without approval of IDA and featuring a
minimum debt-service coverage ratio of 1.25 thereafter.

- 141 -                    ANNEX 6-2
Page 1 of 2
REPUBLIC OF GUINEA
TRANSPORT SECTOR PROJECT
Composante Portuaire/Port Component
PAC -- Tarifs actuels et tarifs propos6s
(PAC -- Existing and Proposed Tariffs)
1.        PAC's tariffs underwent substantial restructuring under the
First Port Project.  Following a consultant's study, a simplified new
tariff structure was put into effect in March 1984, with an average
tariff increase of 15% in addition to earlier increases of 30% in 1983.
The main features of the new structure were:  (a) port dues on ships
(including towage and pilotage charges) calculated on gross registered
tonnage (GRT), plus stevedoring charges, to be paid by the shipping
companies in dollars; and (b) wharf-handling and storage charges, based
on the cargo and billed to the consignee, payable in local currency.
The proportion of PAC's revenues generated by dues on ships was high,
44% compared to the 56% generated by the dues on the cargo.  Compared
with neighboring African ports, PAC's tariffs have been on the high
side, especially taking into account the less than adequate cargo
handling and transit facilities during port rehabilitation, and restric-
tion of ship movements to daytime operation because of the lack of an
operational system of lights and buoys. With the 1986 devaluation, a
revision of the tariffs payable in local currency was needed:  these
were  introduced  in May 1986.   In  accordance with  the  Government's
concern to avoid spiralling domestic price increases, port tariffs in
local currency were raised threefold, substantially less than the
devaluation but still sufficient, as a temporary measure, to protect
PAC's earnings given the relatively small proportion of local costs in
PAC's total expenses. however, proposed tariff adjustments on bauxite
and alumina shipments could not be implemented: the mining companies,
who incurred substantial losses because of insufficient dredging which
allowed only smaller ore-carriers or partially loaded larger ships to
use the port, have refused to pay the tariff increase during 1986.
2.        Further adjustments of the tariff structure were thus required
in 1987 to reflect:   (a) transfer of PAC's stevedoring, shorehandling
and warehousing activities to private sector operators, thereby trans-
forming PAC into an organization dealing essentially with infrastruc-
ture; (b) the changed and evolving structure of the traffic to Conakry
with a higher proportion of large wodern container ships and ro-ro
vessels carrying fast-growing volumes of unitized cargo; and (c) the
necessity to fully recover in the future the cost of the different
investments in the proposed port extension under the project, with
charges corresponding more accurately to the cost of services which the
different users and types of cargo will receive from the new port with
its new installations and institutional set-up.  A tariff study was
therefore carried out by a consultant in late 1986 and early 1987, which
proposed changes in the structure as well as a reasonable increase in
the levels of tariffs. The new structure maintains dues on ships based
on GRT, payable in dollars as before, but with a 30% reduction on dues
for berth occupancy ("droits sur le navire") for container ships and



-142 -                    ANNEX 6-2
Page 2 of 2
ro-ro vessels that have very fast turn-around times.  Ship dues are
constant for stays along berth up to 10 days, but a penalty is charged
beyond 10 days.  Total dues on ships would average about US$1.00 per
ton. The new tariff introduces high charges on cargo ("droits sur la
marcliandise"), payable in local currency differentiated for 25 cate-
gories of cargo; they would range from a low GF 400 per ton on rice to
GP 17,000 per ton on tobacco. Tariffs on alumina and bauxite would be
readjusted to GF 250 and GF 73 per ton, respectively.  Rental fees for
warehouses and open storage areas would be raised substantially to
GF 5,000 and GF 20,000 per ml per year, respectively, which is high but
reflects the real investment costs of these facilities.  Under the new
tariff structure, total dues would vary from about US$1.6 per ton for
minerals and other bulk products, to US$2.7 per ton for oil products and
US$6.5 per ton for general cargo, which is reasonable.  On the whole,
this proposal is satisfactory; as agreed during negotiations, it should
be put into effect at the end of the second quarter of 1987.
3.        PAC does not yet have an analytical cost accounting system to
establish a specific cost-based tariff structure, but reasonable esti-
mates of costs by profit and cost centers are already available and were
used for the tariff study.  As mentioned in Annex 6-1, beyond the 1987
tariff revision, subsequent increases will be required to achieve
financial objectives specified below. Furthermore, PAC will review the
ta.riff structure with the Association by June 1992 at the opening of the
new container terminal, to take into account the development of the
different categories of traffic and the more precise data of the new
cost accounting system, which should be fully operational by then.
WAPTR
April 1987
